Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. The default is -1\n        (the last axis). Only axis=-1 or axis=0 are currently supported for\n        1-D arrays.\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the shape of the output array:\n\n        'valid' (default):\n            Returns output of length N - window_size + 1. The rolling window\n            is only computed where it fully overlaps with the input array.\n\n        'same':\n            Returns output of length N (same as input). The rolling window\n            is padded at the edges to return the same shape as input.\n\n        'full':\n            Returns output of length N + window_size - 1. The rolling window\n            includes partial overlaps at the edges.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array containing the rolling median values with length determined\n        by `mode`. If `a` is an integer or smaller float type, the output\n        dtype is np.float64. Otherwise, the output dtype matches the input.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis\n    numpy.convolve : Returns the discrete, linear convolution\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window that moves across\n    the input array. Each output element is the median of the window at that\n    position.\n\n    This function handles NaN values by including them in the median\n    computation, which may result in NaN outputs.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asarray(a)\n\n    if a.ndim != 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median only supports 1-D arrays\")\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(\"window_size must be an integer\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be at least 1\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    n = len(a)\n\n    # Handle output dtype - n),\n                                     np.arange(window_size) * np.nan,\n                                     np.arange(window_size - n)])\n            padded[window_size - n : window_size - n + n] = a\n            # This is more complex, just handle the padding case\n            output_len = n + window_size - 1\n            result = np.empty(output_len, dtype=dtype)\n            for i in range(output_len):\n                start = max(0, i - window_size + 1)\n                end = min(n, i + 1)\n                result[i] = np.median(a[start:end], dtype=dtype)\n            return result\n\n    # Normal case: window_size <= n\n    output_len_valid = n - window_size + 1\n\n    # Compute rolling median for the valid region\n    valid_result = np.empty(output_len_valid, dtype=dtype)\n    for i in range(output_len_valid):\n        valid_result[i] = np.median(a[i:i + window_size], dtype=dtype)\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return valid_result\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Pad to match input length\n        output_len = n\n        result = np.empty(output_len, dtype=dtype)\n\n        # Left padding\n        left_pad = window_size // 2\n        for i in range(left_pad):\n            result[i] = np.median(a[:i + window_size - left_pad], dtype=dtype)\n\n        # Middle (valid region)\n        result[left_pad:left_pad + output_len_valid] = valid_result\n\n        # Right padding\n        right_pad = window_size - 1 - left_pad\n        for i in range(right_pad):\n            start = n - window_size + 1 + i\n            result[left_pad + output_len_valid + i] = np.median(a[start:], dtype=dtype)\n\n        return result\n    else:  # mode == 'full'\n        output_len = n + window_size - 1\n        result = np.empty(output_len, dtype=dtype)\n\n        for i in range(output_len):\n            start = max(0, i - window_size + 1)\n            end = min(n, i + 1)\n            result[i] = np.median(a[start:end], dtype=dtype)\n\n        return result\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":471,"cache_read_input_tokens":55731,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":471},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d2ff56ee-6b35-4004-8961-73c36c2a2228","uuid":"53cbd103-8053-46f2-a871-065f5ab60abe"}

Only axis=-1 or axis=0 are currently supported for\n        1-D arrays.\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the shape of the output array:\n\n        'valid' (default):\n            Returns output of length N - window_size + 1. The rolling window\n            is only computed where it fully overlaps with the input array.\n\n        'same':\n            Returns output of length N (same as input). The rolling window\n            is padded at the edges to return the same shape as input.\n\n        'full':\n            Returns output of length N + window_size - 1. The rolling window\n            includes partial overlaps at the edges.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array containing the rolling median values with length determined\n        by `mode`. If `a` is an integer or smaller float type, the output\n        dtype is np.float64. Otherwise, the output dtype matches the input.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis\n    numpy.convolve : Returns the discrete, linear convolution\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window that moves across\n    the input array. Each output element is the median of the window at that\n    position.\n\n    This function handles NaN values by including them in the median\n    computation, which may result in NaN outputs.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asarray(a)\n\n    if a.ndim != 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median only supports 1-D arrays\")\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(\"window_size must be an integer\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be at least 1\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    n = len(a)\n\n    # Handle output dtype - Each output element is the median of the window at that\n    position.\n\n    This function handles NaN values by including them in the median\n    computation, which may result in NaN outputs.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asarray(a)\n\n    if a.ndim != 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median only supports 1-D arrays\")\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(\"window_size must be an integer\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be at least 1\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    n = len(a)\n\n    # Handle output dtype - Each output element is the median of the window at that\n    position.\n\n    This function handles NaN values by including them in the median\n    computation, which may result in NaN outputs.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asarray(a)\n\n    if a.ndim != 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"rolling_median only supports 1-D arrays\")\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(\"window_size must be an integer\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be at least 1\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    n = len(a)\n\n    # Handle output dtype -
